### Post by herbster on 2007-10-01
October 2007 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.

* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.

* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.

* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

[COLOR="DarkRed"]*To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:[/COLOR]

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

[color=red]**Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.[/color]**

---

### Post by D-EJ915 on 2007-10-01
Here's mine which I came up with today.  I don't see anyone using CTWM but I have fun with it, if you want to give it a try then you can use this easily enough.

CTWM [system.ctwmrc](http://dej915.serveftp.com/host/DEJ915.chess.ctwmrc)
CTWM theme/pixmaps [Chess](http://gurno.com/adam/ctwm/)
GtkTheme= Bloodline
IconTheme= G-Flat-SVG
Background= [(not sure if anyone wanted it lol but here it is)](http://dej915.serveftp.com/pictures/kowaru_hawt.png)
Programs= Opera, Nautilus --no-desktop, wterm, [mrxvt](http://dej915.serveftp.com/host/mrxvtrc), [xmms](http://dej915.serveftp.com/host/xmms/Cherry-Best.tar.gz), pidgin, µTorrent (wine), wmweather, wminet, wmix, oclock -tr -fg grey32 -bd grey32

[[img]http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v104/enthauptet/bin/th_ctwm_theme_for_mint.png[/img]](http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v104/enthauptet/bin/ctwm_theme_for_mint.png)

### Post by sunexplodes on 2007-10-01
Okay, here goes:
[ATTACH]45050[/ATTACH]
**Distro:** XUbuntu 7.10 Gutsy
**GTK Theme: **[ScaledBlack Murrine](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Scaled+Black+%3A+Murrina+?content=61659)
**Emerald:** [Dreamtiger-Baghira ](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Dream+Tiger+for+Baghira?content=45372)(heavily modified)
**Icons:** [NuevoXT 2](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/nuoveXT+2?content=56625), with some icons mixed in from the new KDE Crystal pack, among a few others. 
**Wallpaper:** [Auros](http://bobbyperux.deviantart.com/art/Auros-Wallpaper-65980603)
**Applications shown:** Sonata, which is a frontend for Music Player Daemon, xfce4-terminal, Avant-Window-Navigator, and Thunar. In the bottom right corner, there is a small, 100% transparent XFCE-Panel, which contains an XKill launcher, Tomboy, a system clock, trash icon, and the system tray. It becomes opaque when moused-over.

### Post by mthei on 2007-10-01
Combination of Clearlooks and Human, with the colours modified (titlebars set to 3d3d3d, so I'll remember  for the next distro I try if I use Gnome) and the gtk set to emulate (rip-off) the dark XP "rainy day" theme, which I used with an assortment of wallpapers previously. Desktop is from drawing up on DeviantArt called "a tear", which reminds me of several album covers that I love. Icons are beautiful [HumanElephant](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/HumanElephant+orange+-+blue?content=67081&PHPSESSID=7bfe99bd359b20cd433a144f0a183655) icons.

### Post by K.Mandla on 2007-10-03

[[img]http://xs319.xs.to/xs319/07394/2007-09-27-193147_800x600_scrot.jpg.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs319&d=07394&f=2007-09-27-193147_800x600_scrot.jpg)

[Celeron laptop]("http://kmandla.wordpress.com/2007/09/24/my-new-thinkpad/") with Openbox 3.4.4 on Arch, using mostly GTK2 apps like Audacious, Kazehakase, Sylpheed, etc. Background is the [popsquares screensaver]("http://kmandla.wordpress.com/2007/09/27/a-clearlooks-popsquares-desktop/"), tweaked for a Tango-esque color pattern. OB theme is a [flattened Clearlooks]("http://kmandla.wordpress.com/2007/09/02/openbox-theme-clearlooks-flat/").

This was an old [K6-2 laptop]("http://kmandla.wordpress.com/2007/09/13/gtk12-doesnt-have-to-be-ugly/") that I "borrowed" from a shelf at work. At the time it was running Gutsy with only GTK1.2 applications. Ugly as sin, but amazingly fast for a 450Mhz machine. 

[[img]http://xs219.xs.to/xs219/07374/2007-09-13-075740_1024x768_scrot.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs219&d=07374&f=2007-09-13-075740_1024x768_scrot.png)

GTK themes were set to Mist. OB theme was the same flattened Clearlooks, if I recall correctly. Background was #3465a4, set with *xsetroot*.

### Post by R-Dot-Yung on 2007-10-03
> **~LoKe said:**
> You can repay me by posting your conkyrc. :D

Anything for such a big NIN fan, haha, i feel like you have every song ever made by them, i only have every retail CD (digitally)

```
#avoid flicker
double_buffer yes

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys
own_window  yes
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type normal
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

#borders
draw_borders no
border_margin 1
draw_graph_borders no

#shades
draw_shades no
  
#position
gap_x 0
gap_y 0
alignment top_left
  
#behaviour
update_interval 1
  
#colour
default_color  gray
 
#default_shade_color 000000
own_window_colour 333333
 
#font
use_xft yes
xftfont Dejavu Sans:pixelsize=9
 
#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer no
minimum_size 1600 0
 
#mpd
mpd_host localhost
mpd_port 6600
  
TEXT
Time: ${color white}${time %d %B} ${color white}${time  %H:%M} ${color} Up: ${color white}${uptime_short}${color} Cpu: ${color white}${cpu}%${color} ${cpugraph 8,50 white} Processes: ${color white}$processes  ${color}Running: ${color white}$running_processes ${color} Mem: ${color white}$mem/$memmax ${color} ${memgraph 8,50 white}${color white} ${color }Net: ${color white}${downspeed wlan0} Kb/s${color}  ${downspeedgraph wlan0 9,50 white} ${color white}${upspeed wlan0} Kb/s ${color} ${upspeedgraph wlan0 8,50 white} Hda: ${color white}${fs_free /}/${fs_size /} ${color} Hdb: ${color white}${fs_free /home}/${fs_size /home}${color} MPD: ${color white}${mpd_smart}
```

Zing

---

### Post by adamorjames on 2007-10-04
Well I apt-get'd conky... now the problem is how to get it to work with Flux Box. Any ideas? Right now it says it's running but nothing shows,I guess just make a quick reply back to me or PM me since this isn't really the right thread. Thanks.

---

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2007-10-04
> **adamorjames said:**
> Well I apt-get'd conky... now the problem is how to get it to work with Flux Box. Any ideas? Right now it says it's running but nothing shows,I guess just make a quick reply back to me or PM me since this isn't really the right thread. Thanks.

In the terminal type
```
gedit ~/.conkyrc
```

and post the following in it.

```

# conky config
# edited by notwen @ efnet

# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background yes

# X font when Xft is disabled, you can pick one with program xfontsel
#font 5x7
#font 6x10
#font 7x13
#font 8x13
#font 9x15
#font *mintsmild.se*
#font -*-*-*-*-*-*-34-*-*-*-*-*-*-*


# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
#xftfont Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:size=8
xftfont Terminus:size=8

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 0.8

# Print everything to console?
# out_to_console no

# mail spool
#mail_spool $MAIL

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1.0

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes

# If own_window is yes, you may use type normal, desktop or override
own_window_type override

# Use pseudo transparency with own_window?
own_window_transparent yes

# If own_window_transparent is set to no, you can set the background
colour here
#own_window_colour hotpink

# If own_window is yes, these window manager hints may be used
#own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 130 5

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 5

# border margins
border_margin 5
# UBUNTU-CONKY
# A comprehensive conky script, configured for use on
# Ubuntu / Debian Gnome, without the need for any external scripts.
#
# Based on conky-jc and the default .conkyrc.
# INCLUDES:
# - tail of /var/log/messages 
# - netstat connections to your computer
#
# -- Pengo (conky@pengo.us)
#

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,skip_taskbar
background no

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# fiddle with window
use_spacer yes
use_xft yes

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1.5

# Minimum size of text area
#minimum_size 400 5

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Text stuff
draw_outline no # amplifies text if yes
draw_borders no

uppercase no # set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 8

# border margins
border_margin 4

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors, grey90 == #e5e5e5
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white

own_window_colour brown
own_window_transparent yes

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
gap_x 10
gap_y 10

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

override_utf8_locale no
xftfont Terminus:size=8
xftalpha 0.8

TEXT
${font malayalam:bold:size=10}+--Date/Time
|    |
|   +--${time %a, } ${color }${time %B %e %G}
|   +--${time %I:%M:%S %P}
|
+--System
|    |
|   +--cpu - ${cpu cpu1}%, ${color }${cpugraph cpu1 8,60 000000 000000}
|   +--cpu temp - ${acpitemp}C
|   +--ram - $mem/$memmax - $memperc%
|   +--battery - ${battery}
|   +--signal - ${linkstatus eth1} %
|
+--Network
     |
    +--down - ${downspeed eth1} k/s ${downspeedgraph eth1 8,60 000000 000000}
    +--up - ${upspeed eth1} k/s ${upspeedgraph eth1 8,60 000000 000000}

```

Then do a killall conky and and run conky again.

### Post by ~LoKe on 2007-10-04
> **R-Dot-Yung said:**
> wish i knew how to use MPD :(

```
sudo apt-get install mpd mpc ncmpc gmpc sonata
```
```
sudo ln -s $HOME/mp3s /usr/share/mpd/music ## Make sure you change $HOME/mp3s to the path of your music
```
```
mpc update
```

Then you can just type in "ncmpc" into the terminal.  Or, open up Sonata and play that way.

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2007-10-04
> **Stan_1936 said:**
> What;s your conky setup?  could you post it?Sure thing. As requested, here's my conkyrc:
> 
own_window no
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
use_xft yes
update_interval 0.5
draw_shades no
draw_borders no
xftfont MOn NOm Mono:pixelsize=11.5
minimum_size 1280 0
border_margin 1
default_color 200001
alignment bottom_left
gap_x 15
gap_y 10
TEXT
${font MOn NOm Mono:size=18}${time %b %d}                           ${time %I:%M %p}$font
Core 1:${cpugraph cpu0 8,50}$color                                                          Dubai-${color 200001}${execi 100 /home/melski/scripts/weather/weather.sh "MEA|AE|AE005|DUBAI"}
Core 2:${cpugraph cpu1 8,50}$color                                                              HDD:${color 200001}${fs_free_perc}% free          
Uptime:${color 200001}${uptime}$color               Kernel:${color 200001}${kernel}  ${execi 30 acpi -b}

Just adjust the spacing - see thumbnail - (needs tinkering & patience :)). And, the link to the excellent font:

[http://www.smeltery.net/smeltery.html](http://www.smeltery.net/smeltery.html) :guitar:

### Post by santiagoward2000 on 2007-10-04
> **ArtF10 said:**
> Details?  Theme, wallpaper, fonts?

Sure! The theme and icons are Nuvola, from the gnome-extra-icons package. I changed the font's background color through the gtkrc-2.0 file ([http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=3197338&postcount=435]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=3197338&postcount=435")). I set the icons size at 82 and the text size at 12.
I downloaded the wallpaper from [http://www.xfce-look.org/]("http://www.xfce-look.org/").
I haven't changed the fonts actually, it's Sans 9.
The Screenlets Sidebar uses the curved theme. The clock is actually Cairo-Clock, I just copied the Station theme from the Screenlet's clock.
I use Compiz-Fusion with Emerald. The Emerald theme is VRunner Quicksilver. I found the cube's caps on Google. The skydome was downloaded from [http://taint.org/xplanet/]("http://taint.org/xplanet/") (I'm not sure if the page is still there).
The icon's on Kiba-Dock were collected from around the web, mostly looking in Google. The Clock plugin uses Cairo's glassy theme.
The upper panel is set at size 38%, transparency 20%. I removed the "Applications" text and used the image downloaded from.
I put a transparent xfce4-terminal on the desktop, setting it's transparency shade level to none, and turning the "Show Window Borders" and "Show menubar" off. That cool-looking messenger is gaim-text (I haven't upgraded to Pidgin/Finch). I just love it, way better than using Gaim with its gui!!!
Firefox's theme is Kempleton.
I think I mentioned everything. If there's anything else you want to know, just ask!

By the way, all desktops in this thread look so cool!!

---

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2007-10-05
> **herbster said:**
> Thank you, those are nice fonts! However, I just changed my Active Window title font to a few of those via Obconf, and the titlebar is changing to the font but they are not going all caps :confused:I experienced the same issue but what I did was I edited my fluxstyle (my WM: fluxbox btw), and changed to the font name.

An excerpt from my current fluxstyle (tylerdurden's):
> *font:   			AvantGarde LT Medium-8
window.font: AvantGarde LT Medium-8
toolbar.clock.font: AvantGarde LT Medium-8
toolbar.workspace.font: AvantGarde LT Medium-8
toolbar.iconbar.focused.font: AvantGarde LT Medium-8
toolbar.iconbar.unfocused.font: AvantGarde LT Medium-8


Hope this helps.

---

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2007-10-05
[QUOTE=rjmdomingo2003;3478224]I experienced the same issue but what I did was I edited my fluxstyle (my WM: fluxbox btw), and changed to the font name.

BTW, the font name you incorporate into your style shouldn't necessarily be the file name. When I open the font file using Gnome's font viewer, the font name indicated on the window title is the name I put into my style. It isn't always the file name.

Ex: font file name: AvantGardeGothicLTMediumCAPS.ttf
      _actual font name_: Avant Garde LT Medium

In this example, you put the actual font name into your style.

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-10-05
> **el mariachi said:**
> Awsome! I was looking for something like this to freshen and soothe my old desktop pc. The XFCE-panel suits it really well. Will you release it?
*I need to start digging your code to learn how to theme right:lolflag:*

Thanks. I've uploaded the Openbox theme to box-look ([here]("http://box-look.org/content/show.php?content=67434")) and the gtk theme, which uses the Murrine engine, to gnome-look ([here]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=67435")).

Making themes in Openbox is pretty simple, actually, and one of the many reasons why I like it so much. Just play around with the various settings until you come to something you like. [Agave]("http://home.gna.org/colorscheme/") is a great tool to make sure the colours match.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2007-10-07

### Post by ryno519 on 2007-10-07
I can't remember where I got the wallpaper from, I think from the Art Manager that comes with Gutsy, but it might have been gnome-look. I'm using the human window borders and the clearlooks controls with custom colours (light green).

I got rid of the minimize button on the Windows because I don't like using the taskbar. Compiz fusion has many more interesting ways to organize and access your various windows and I prefer just using the scale plugin with bottom-right corner access.

I'm using the tango icon theme because I couldn't find any good greenish themes on gnome-look. They're alright, but it's the one thing I'm not 100% happy with with this setup.

I'm always amazed how 10 minutes of little tweaks can transform your desktop into a very attractive, unique experience.

---

### Post by John.Michael.Kane on 2007-10-09
> **herbster said:**
> What would be the commands to add Restart and Shutdown options to my Openbox menu ??
You can try the ones below.
sudo shutdown -t now
sudo init 0 #Shutdown 
sudo reboot 
sudo init 6 #Reboot

[http://linux.byexamples.com/archives/87/using-gui-dialog-box/](http://linux.byexamples.com/archives/87/using-gui-dialog-box/)

Note you would have to edit you /etc/sudoers file to do it without root password.

### Post by arbulus on 2007-10-10
> **Opeth115 said:**
> Wow... that is one of the nicest desktop i have EVER seen...  I don't have any applets like that for awn though and i compiled from svn why is that?  please tell me your wallpaper and ur emerald theme too!

You need to get the Bazaar version, not the SVN version.  Completely remove the SVN version, then install the BZR version as well as awn extras to get the applets.

Here's a link explaining how to install:
[http://www.planetblur.org/hosted/awnforum/index.php?shard=forum&action=g_reply&ID=539&page=1&isLive=true](http://www.planetblur.org/hosted/awnforum/index.php?shard=forum&action=g_reply&ID=539&page=1&isLive=true)

Here's how to install the AWN Extras:
[http://awn.wetpaint.com/page/AWN-Extras?t=anon](http://awn.wetpaint.com/page/AWN-Extras?t=anon)

I don't seem to have the menu in xfce-panel, what applet is it?

Thank you, mariachi. 

The applet called -- guess what -- 'xfce4-menu-plugin'. I believe it is installed automatically with the xfce-panel (from source as I did, or through the repos). In the 'add to panel' dialog, it is called 'xfce menu'. Keep in mind though that I have customised it (right click > Properties). The default title/text (I believe it is normally 'Start' or 'Applications') as well as the default icon are different.

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-10-11
> **el mariachi said:**
> can the panel's color be changed without touching the rest of the GTK theme?
and font size too btw 

thanks urukrama!

weird I don't have that applet... I'll dig into it.

This is how you can change your panel in xfce4:

Make a .gtkrc-2.0 and put it in your /home/folder

This is one that I used with the image "stripe_autum.png" when I was on xubuntu 7.04:

```

style "panel"
{
  bg[NORMAL] = "#595553"
  bg_pixmap[NORMAL] = "stripe_autum.png"
  fg[NORMAL] = "#FFFFFF"
  }

widget_class "*Panel*"      style "panel"
widget "*Panel*"            style "panel"
class "*Panel*"             style "panel"


```


...then just put your image in your /home/folder along with your .gtkrc-2.0 file


Now if you just want a color change, then edit out the "bg_pixmap[NORMAL] part with the image...and just make your bg[NORMAL] the color you want it to be...and the fg[NORMAL] is your font color.


There are other ways to change the buttons, font size and other things, but I'm not sure because I was always doing it for panel image.

### Post by tschneiter on 2007-10-16
Details - 
Running xcompmgr for compositing, with avant-window-navigator for a dock. Conky is over there on the right (will provide config if anyone asks). 
The dock isn't at the bottom of the screen because I am running a dual-monitor setup, and the primary does 1440x900, whereas the secondary does 1280x1024.   It all looks proper on the actual screens.

Theming - 
Controls - Clearlooks_cairo-gPerfect
Window Border - MinimiLista
Icons - HumanAzul2

The background I actually found in this thread somewhere. Uhhm, I think thats about it! I am a bit sad that I cannot run DRI with an intel card, as my resolution is over 2048... I could, if I wanted a vertical layout for the external monitor, but that just seems silly.


Anyways, theres that!

### Post by undine on 2007-10-18
> **m.musashi said:**
> Been a while since I posted a screenshot.

Here is my gutsy desktop:
[http://ubuntukids.org/blog/wp-content/uploads/2007/10/gutsy_release2.png](http://ubuntukids.org/blog/wp-content/uploads/2007/10/gutsy_release2.png)

And here is my gutsy laptop:
[http://ubuntukids.org/blog/wp-content/uploads/2007/10/gutsy_laptop.png](http://ubuntukids.org/blog/wp-content/uploads/2007/10/gutsy_laptop.png)

Sorry, I don't know how to make those into thumbnails. I'll edit if someone can explain.

You can make thumbnails in the following way: take the original screenshot, open it in GIMP, resize the largest dimension of the image down to 200 or 200 pixels. Save this resized image as screenshot01-th.png (or whatever). Upload both the original and thumbnailed image somewhere, then use the following code to post:

<url=http://ubuntukids.org/blog/wp-content/uploads/2007/10/screenshot01.png><img>http://ubuntukids.org/blog/wp-content/uploads/2007/10/screenshot1-th.png</img></url> 

Of course you will have to use [ instead of < when it comes to actual posting... sorry I hat to enter it that way, the <code> tag doesn't appear to be working for whatever reason.

Now, if you'd be so kind as to provide the details of your theme there, as I like it quite a lot ;)

### Post by Kappity on 2007-10-19
Here's how mine looks with 800x600 resolution.

I couldn't remember for sure what maximum resolution this old laptop would support.  After some research at Thinkwiki.org and elsewhere, I've discovered that 800x600 is indeed the max possible for the Thinkpad A20m with 12.1 inch screen.  No more messing around with xorg.conf.  This is it.

Feisty 7.04.  Mist theme, which is part of the standard release.

[Here is]("http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2292/1641236055_ddf2a9f3ff_o.png") the bare desktop.  The Wallpaper is M.C. Escher's woodcut "Day and Night", available from, I dunno, there are plenty of Escher sites, and I've had this file for a while.

[In use]("http://farm3.static.flickr.com/2101/1641236069_ac420651c4_o.png").  The program is Scid 3.6.1, a chess database downloadable through Synaptic package manager.  For those who don't play chess seriously, this is a tool for managing large game collections for study, not primarily a chess playing program.  Here's where the low screen resolution is a small problem.  It would be nice to see some of these windows side by side, but they can't be sized smaller than this.

Well, this old computer has been resurrected as my platform for learning Ubuntu.  Some day I'll get to see how it works on a better system.

8)

### Post by shearn89 on 2007-10-20
> **b4t3m4n said:**
> I can't seem to get conky or pypanel to load a ttf font I downloaded and installed.  I am pretty sure I installed it correctly because I can select it as a font in my appearance settings in gnome.

Firstly make sure the name you're using is exactly right - its not the same as the filename. If you double click on the font file you can see the actual name.
Secondly, i installed conky from source (i think), but its version 1.4.7. Make sure thats the same.
Thirdly, in pypanel, make sure the font is in " " if it has spaces in its name.

I'm also running gutsy, so if you haven't upgraded yet, it could be that?

EDIT: Oh, and make sure you restart them once you've changed the rc file. I use
 ```
kill $(pgrep conky); conky
#and
kill $(pgrep pypanel); pypanel &

```

Or you can just logout and in.

---

### Post by BrettRS on 2007-10-20
> **rjmdomingo2003 said:**
> Could you post your tintrc file? Thanks.

```
font = gelly
font_color = #FFFFFF
font_alpha = 0
font_active_color = #FFFFFF
font_active_alpha = 0
font_shadow = 1
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 100
task_margin = 3
task_padding = 5
panel_width = 1000
panel_height = 25
panel_tasks_centered = 0
panel_background = 1
panel_background_color = #ffffff
panel_background_alpha = 0
task_background = 1
task_background_color = #000000
task_background_alpha = 10
task_active_background_color = #C08275
task_active_background_alpha = 70
task_background_as_border = 0
```

### Post by b4t3m4n on 2007-10-20
> **shearn89 said:**
> Firstly make sure the name you're using is exactly right - its not the same as the filename. If you double click on the font file you can see the actual name.
Secondly, i installed conky from source (i think), but its version 1.4.7. Make sure thats the same.
Thirdly, in pypanel, make sure the font is in " " if it has spaces in its name.

I'm also running gutsy, so if you haven't upgraded yet, it could be that?

EDIT: Oh, and make sure you restart them once you've changed the rc file. I use
 ```
kill $(pgrep conky); conky
#and
kill $(pgrep pypanel); pypanel &

```

Or you can just logout and in.



Okay, I have pypanel working with it now.  Conky is still not taking it.  I also tried to use Impact with conky as well, something simple.  It didn't work either.  I am using amd64 gutsy, is the conky from the sources not the right version?

### Post by Vansinnesvisan on 2007-10-21
> **Opeth115 said:**
> i love your desktops lol.  I have one question, for your background how did u get it to look so nice?  even the downloaded size of that image gets stretched beyond oblivion.

I used gimp to center the image on a 1680x1050 template, then extruded a 1 pixel thick copy of the images edges to fill in the rest. Then blurred it. 

Kind of sloppy, but I am far too lazy and fickle to make it look all proper.

### Post by Mazza558 on 2007-10-21
> **misfitpierce said:**
> Im curious to know why ppl are still posting upon request crap on themes. I think its pretty well stated 

So I dont know how about we just include them inside screenshot or in forum auto instead of having to ask. 

Oh and nice desktop.

It's because I prefer to wait and see if anyone's interested before posting theme details. In my case, there was a LOT of tweaking done to get my desktop to look like this, and I'd rather people just ask things like "wow, how did you get that gradient gnome panel?" or "what's that file browser?" - this is because it's unlikely that anyone wants exactly the same desktop as me - most people just ask for specific parts of the theme.

---

### Post by Vansinnesvisan on 2007-10-21
> **Mazza558 said:**

In my case, there was a LOT of tweaking done to get my desktop to look like this, and I'd rather people just ask things like "wow, how did you get that gradient gnome panel?" or "what's that file browser?" - this is because it's unlikely that anyone wants exactly the same desktop as me - most people just ask for specific parts of the theme.

You could grab a script that prints out all your themes/fonts/DE/etc in a terminal. There are a lot of them, but here is an old one: [http://forum.beryl-project.org/viewtopic.php?f=51&t=5448](http://forum.beryl-project.org/viewtopic.php?f=51&t=5448)

May not list every detail, but gets most things.

### Post by m.musashi on 2007-10-21
> **adamorjames said:**
> The script. I did install the packages. It shows that I'm using all Human for my theme and I'm not.

I'm afraid I don't know much about the script. I didn't write it. However, it poles gconf for the info. I'd check the keys in gconf and see what they say. Specifically, check this part...
```
  echo "GTK2:     `gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/gtk_theme`"
  echo "Metacity:           `gconftool-2 --get /apps/metacity/general/theme`"
  echo "Icons:              `gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/icon_theme`"
```
If the info in the keys doesn't match then I'd say something odd is going on. Or maybe the script is missing things because you have set up your system differently. Maybe tweaking the script would help. Unfortunately, I don't know how to do that.

---

### Post by m.musashi on 2007-10-22
> **Scruffynerf said:**
> Depends on how you run it.

I've just installed the script from ubuntukids, and if I run it as sudo/location/info.sh it shows human, because that is the themes for root.

Ran it as just myself, /location/info.sh and it shows fine.

Maybe I should add the rest of the directions. Sorry. First, you have to chmod it
```
chmod +x info.sh
```
No need to use sudo as it's in your /home and your file (i.e. not root's). Assuming it's in your /home (i.e. no subfolders) run it like this
```
./info.sh
```
Guess I'll add that to the site. If you run it as root then I guess it's possible to get theme info for root.

EDIT: okay, just to clean up my mess, here is a post that should tie up any loose ends --> [http://ubuntukids.org/blog/?p=43](http://ubuntukids.org/blog/?p=43)

### Post by Retrograde77 on 2007-10-23
> **shearn89 said:**
> Hey - do the icons for soundcard/headset just change the volume, or do other stuff as well? How does it work?

I have Medusa 5.1 USB headphones, so what those scripts do is change the default sound card.  Windows has software that auto switches to the headphones which doesn't exist for Linux, so when I want to switch I just run the script :)

Everything then runs from the headphones, except flash which is odd, but what the hell lol.

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-10-23
> **notwen said:**
> What are you doin in GNOME dood?!?!?!

You noticed, haha!


Well, I installed Archlinux 2007.08-2, and I tried out the new Gnome 2.20... since I've only used xfce4 for my first year on Linux.


I found out that I like certain things... like the transparent panel, and the look of Nautilus. I also liked my system sounds, and the look of the Glossy clearlooks buttons/tabs and how it looks in my Applications Menu/Places/System...


I also tried xfce4 on Archlinux and I had a problem with the top panel not allowing me to remove it with out crashing both panels. Then when I would start "xfce4-panle &", the top panel was not deleted.


I think that Gnome on Archlinux feels about as fast as xfce4 on xubuntu, and it has this solid stable feel to it... unless I open way too many apps at once. 


I'll see how it feels when I install Compiz Fusion 0.6.0.... and if it is slower, I will go back to xfce4. I do think xfce4 handles a few things better... like the custom commands in Thunar seem more usable than Nautilus scripts... but I'm still getting used to Gnome and I'm sure there are some good Nautilus scripts out there.

---

### Post by Vansinnesvisan on 2007-10-23
> **crimesaucer said:**
> 

I also tried xfce4 on Archlinux and I had a problem with the top panel not allowing me to remove it with out crashing both panels. Then when I would start "xfce4-panle &", the top panel was not deleted.

That seems to be a common problem. Manually editing panels.xml under ~/.config/xfce4/panel/ will allow to to remove the panel without issue. 

Annoying bug though. Is it only on Arch?

> **Scruffynerf said:**

---

### Post by Scruffynerf on 2007-10-24
> **n3tfury said:**
> what script are you using for the terminal output?

Original found at [http://ubuntukids.org/blog/]("http://ubuntukids.org/blog/")

I've tweaked it from the original above to include the background info from gconf, however it displays the path & filename. I'd like to trim it to just the filename, but I don't know how.

Script references a "iphitus" however I've no idea who he is.

Mine as follows:

The dependencies:

```
sudo apt-get install indent scrot
```

The code:

```
#!/bin/bash
#####
##### iphitus' screenshot script :D
#####
#####RENAME THIS FILE EXTENSION FROM .txt to .sh
#####-edit as needed
#####-execute from a terminal or run dialog with
#####sh info.sh

# screenshot dir
ssdir="/home/<your username>/"
# screenshot description
ssdesc="/home/<your username>"
# screenshot format
ss=`date +%d%m%Y`.png

# Extra hdd details?
hdddetails=1
# Use comments file?
comments=0
# Automatically grab gnome theme info
autognome=1

#echo
#date
echo
echo "Kernel:         `uname -r`"
#echo "Distro:         `cat /etc/*release`"
. /etc/lsb-release
echo "Distro:         $DISTRIB_ID $DISTRIB_RELEASE $DISTRIB_CODENAME"
echo "Uptime:         `uptime |cut --delimiter=" " -f 2`"
echo ___________________________________________________________________
echo "CPU:           `grep "model name" /proc/cpuinfo|cut --delimiter=":" -f 2`" 
echo "Speed:         `grep "cpu MHz" /proc/cpuinfo|cut --delimiter=":" -f 2` mhz"
echo "Bogomips:      `grep "bogomips" /proc/cpuinfo|cut --delimiter=":" -f 2` bogomips"
echo ___________________________________________________________________
let memtotal=`grep "MemTotal" /proc/meminfo|cut -c 12-22|indent -i0`/1024
echo "Memory Total:   $memtotal mb"
let memfree=`grep "MemFree" /proc/meminfo|cut -c 12-22|indent -i0`/1024
let memcache=`grep "Cached" /proc/meminfo|cut -c 12-22|indent -i0`
let memcache=$memcache/1024
let memfreetotal=$memfree+$memcache
echo "Memory Free:    $memfreetotal mb"
echo ___________________________________________________________________
#echo "Graphics:       `grep "Product" /proc/fb0/vbe_info|cut --delimiter=" " -f 5`" 
cat /proc/driver/nvidia/version
echo ___________________________________________________________________
if [ $autognome == 1 ]; then
  echo "GTK2:           		`gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/gtk_theme`"
  echo "Metacity:                       `gconftool-2 --get /apps/metacity/general/theme`"
  echo "Icons:          		`gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/icon_theme`"
  echo "Titlebar Font:      		`gconftool-2 --get /apps/metacity/general/titlebar_font`"
  echo "Application Font:  		`gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/font_name`"
  echo "Terminal Font:  		`gconftool-2 --get /apps/gnome-terminal/profiles/Default/font`"
  echo "Background:			`gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/background/picture_filename`"
fi
sleep 4
scrot $ss
echo
exit 0
```

Also, you need to set the script as an executable.

Edit: Running the script will also wait for 4 seconds, then automatically take a screenshot for you as well. It's a nifty little script. There's some discussion of it on page 72-74 of this thread.

### Post by John.Michael.Kane on 2007-10-25
> **herbster said:**
> Is it possible to take a screenshot of my home pc remotely, ie., via ssh? I just tried scrot in an ssh session but it said "Can't open X display."

You can try the below method.

First verify you have enabled X forwarding on your ssh server, i.e. check sshd_config for:
```
X11Forwarding yes
```

After you are connected to your server before running import, run:
```
export DISPLAY=localhost:0.0
```
Or whatever the display your target X server is running on.

Followed by your import.

---

### Post by herbster on 2007-10-26
> **SD-Plissken said:**
> You can try the below method.

First verify you have enabled X forwarding on your ssh server, i.e. check sshd_config for:
```
X11Forwarding yes
```

After you are connected to your server before running import, run:
```
export DISPLAY=localhost:0.0
```
Or whatever the display your target X server is running on.

Followed by your import.

```
bobby:~$ export DISPLAY=localhost:0.0
bobby:~$ d
bobby:~/Desktop$ import ss.jpg
import: unable to open X server `localhost:0.0'.
```

My computer (the one I'm connected to in SSH with, that I want to take a SS of) is using dual monitors. I'm currently on a Vista laptop. If this helps.

---

### Post by John.Michael.Kane on 2007-10-26
> **herbster said:**
> ```
bobby:~$ export DISPLAY=localhost:0.0
bobby:~$ d
bobby:~/Desktop$ import ss.jpg
import: unable to open X server `localhost:0.0'.
```

My computer (the one I'm connected to in SSH with, that I want to take a SS of) is using dual monitors. I'm currently on a Vista laptop. If this helps.

From what I can find on this subject here is what you can try. 

You would first need to know the identity of the window or windows used by application 'Z' on X server at 'A'. You should be able to use xwininfo to find this info. Once you know the identity of the window, You should then be able to use xwd to grab the specified window to an image file (you might have pass the image through a conversion tool like Imagemagick, to convert your image to a desired format). 

The 'specified window' should exist on any X server that's reachable, and is accepting connections from the host 'B'. The xwd tool should run on host 'B', however should communicate with the X server on host 'A' using this scenario. 

The X server at 'A' would need to allow this communication (man xhost, xauth).

---

I really like this, and want to know how to make it start with certain things running. I can say that if anyone tries this, and feels thwarted upon reaching the desktop, then press both mouse buttons (or the middle one) to bring up a menu.

I also understand there's some way to have it run instead of metacity in gnome, but I'm afraid to mess with that yet. If I can just customize it in it's own environment, I'd be happy for now.

### Post by IIIV on 2007-10-28
> **Sain said:**
> Does AWN iconst still go behind panel when you click on it?

 I had similar desktop, but gave up on AWN since I couldn't make it to be always in front of my gnome panel.


Yes, my AWN dock is always on top of the Gnome Panel... Here's how to do it:


1. Install devilspie:

```
sudo apt-get install devilspie
```

2. Create a devilspie directory:

```
mkdir ~/.devilspie
```

3. Create AWN .ds file:

```
gksudo gedit ~/.devilspie/awn.ds
```

4. Put this code then save:

```
(if (is (application_name) "avant-window-navigator") (above))
```

5. Add [FONT="Courier New"]devilspie[/FONT] in your autostart sessions:

System -> Settings -> Sessions


6. Restart your computer and check if it works.  :-)


Credits to: [happy-and-lost]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=3370460&postcount=16")

### Post by urukrama on 2007-10-29
I'm back on my other computer, and I realise how different colours can look on different screens! My [very white setup]("http://www.diegrossestille.de/english/"), for example, that looked perfectly beautiful and clean on my second computer, looks awefully bright and painful on this old laptop. I apologize for the pain I must have caused to the eyes of some forum members... :( I now understand your pain.

So I am back to a darker wallpaper and window decorations (I can never really get used to fully dark themes, so the applcitions themselves have to look reasonably light).

Here are the details: Openbox 3.4, Openbox and gtk theme are Dandelion, fonts are HeldustryFTVBasicBlack (Window headers), Sans (Openbox Menu) and Yataghan (conky). Wallpaper is based on a screenshot from the documentary *[Into Great Silence]("http://www.diegrossestille.de/english/")*

### Post by svtfmook on 2007-10-30
> **CoolDreamZ said:**
> WOW! That last one is amazing. What theme etc did you use?
the theme is completely custom.  controls are amaranth, icons are mostly sladf, but quite a few are mixed/matched from all icon themes.  comic fonts throughout the desktop and swift font used in places.  AWN w/ swift fonts and true glass theme.  gnome-color-chooser is used for the font color on the panel and desktop icons.  modified gtkc 2.0 config file to remove panel separators.  then conky.  compiz-fusion w/ skydome.

### Post by sistoviejo on 2007-11-01
Theme: Star Dust (modified)
[http://themes.beryl-project.org/theme_details.php?id=73](http://themes.beryl-project.org/theme_details.php?id=73)

Wallpaper: Found on google/somehow/don't remember. :) 

Icons: Jini icon theme
[http://art.gnome.org/themes/icon/1138](http://art.gnome.org/themes/icon/1138)

Programs:
1 - Emerald Theme Manager. (Installed through Synaptics)
2 - gDesklets 0.35 (starterbar, osxclock, ftbcpu, ftbmemory, ftbinfo, ftbnet)
3 - Compiz fusion's water effect on fifth image.
4 - Compiz fusion's Desktop cube on last two images.


The OS X like icon bar is starterbar for gdesklets. gdesklets can be installed using synaptics. starterbar comes included in the package. If you're using Ubuntu 7.10 for x64, you'll need to install a .deb fix to make gdesklets work. You can read about this and download the fix here: [https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/gdesklets/+bug/110103](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/gdesklets/+bug/110103) (Look for this file: gdesklets_0.35.4-1ubuntu1_amd64.deb)

Screenshots:

[[IMG]http://img454.imageshack.us/img454/3625/screenshotwc9.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img454.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshotwc9.jpg) [[IMG]http://img187.imageshack.us/img187/3158/screenshot1sd8.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img187.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshot1sd8.jpg) [[IMG]http://img502.imageshack.us/img502/6172/screenshot2ya3.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img502.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshot2ya3.jpg) 
[[IMG]http://img484.imageshack.us/img484/4517/screenshot3tj0.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img484.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshot3tj0.jpg) [[IMG]http://img102.imageshack.us/img102/3941/screenshot4ft7.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img102.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshot4ft7.jpg) [[IMG]http://img102.imageshack.us/img102/3039/screenshot5sp8.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img102.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshot5sp8.jpg)
